<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations_and_military">Foreign relations and military</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Afghanistan" title="Foreign relations of Afghanistan">Foreign relations of Afghanistan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Afghan_Armed_Forces" title="Afghan Armed Forces">Afghan Armed Forces</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:First_set_of_Afghan_UH-60A_Black_Hawks.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/First_set_of_Afghan_UH-60A_Black_Hawks.jpg/220px-First_set_of_Afghan_UH-60A_Black_Hawks.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="139" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/First_set_of_Afghan_UH-60A_Black_Hawks.jpg/330px-First_set_of_Afghan_UH-60A_Black_Hawks.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/First_set_of_Afghan_UH-60A_Black_Hawks.jpg/440px-First_set_of_Afghan_UH-60A_Black_Hawks.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5187" data-file-height="3282" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:First_set_of_Afghan_UH-60A_Black_Hawks.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Sikorsky_UH-60_Black_Hawk" title="Sikorsky UH-60 Black Hawk">Black Hawks</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Afghan_Air_Force" title="Afghan Air Force">Afghan Air Force</a> at <a href="/wiki/Kandahar_International_Airport" title="Kandahar International Airport">Kandahar Airfield</a>. As a <a href="/wiki/Major_non-NATO_ally" title="Major non-NATO ally">major non-NATO ally</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Afghan_Armed_Forces" title="Afghan Armed Forces">Afghan Armed Forces</a> receive most of their equipment and <a href="/wiki/Resolute_Support_Mission" title="Resolute Support Mission">training</a> from the <a href="/wiki/Afghanistan%E2%80%93United_States_relations" title="Afghanistan–United States relations">United States</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>Afghanistan became a member of the United Nations in 1946. It enjoys cordial relations with a number of <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a> and allied nations, particularly the <a href="/wiki/Afghanistan%E2%80%93United_States_relations" title="Afghanistan–United States relations">United States</a>, <a href="/wiki/Afghanistan%E2%80%93Canada_relations" title="Afghanistan–Canada relations">Canada</a>, <a href="/wiki/Afghanistan%E2%80%93United_Kingdom_relations" title="Afghanistan–United Kingdom relations">United Kingdom</a>, <a href="/wiki/Afghanistan%E2%80%93Germany_relations" title="Afghanistan–Germany relations">Germany</a>, Australia, and <a href="/wiki/Afghanistan%E2%80%93Turkey_relations" title="Afghanistan–Turkey relations">Turkey</a>. In 2012, the United States and Afghanistan signed their <a href="/wiki/U.S.%E2%80%93Afghanistan_Strategic_Partnership_Agreement" title="U.S.–Afghanistan Strategic Partnership Agreement">Strategic Partnership Agreement</a> in which Afghanistan became a <a href="/wiki/Major_non-NATO_ally" title="Major non-NATO ally">major non-NATO ally</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193">&#91;193&#93;</a></sup> Afghanistan also has friendly diplomatic relations with neighboring <a href="/wiki/Afghanistan%E2%80%93China_relations" title="Afghanistan–China relations">China</a>, <a href="/wiki/Afghanistan%E2%80%93Iran_relations" title="Afghanistan–Iran relations">Iran</a>, <a href="/wiki/Afghanistan%E2%80%93Pakistan_relations" title="Afghanistan–Pakistan relations">Pakistan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Afghanistan%E2%80%93Tajikistan_relations" title="Afghanistan–Tajikistan relations">Tajikistan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Turkmenistan#Afghanistan" title="Foreign relations of Turkmenistan">Turkmenistan</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Uzbekistan" title="Foreign relations of Uzbekistan">Uzbekistan</a>, including with regional states such as <a href="/wiki/Afghanistan%E2%80%93Bangladesh_relations" title="Afghanistan–Bangladesh relations">Bangladesh</a>, <a href="/wiki/Afghanistan%E2%80%93India_relations" title="Afghanistan–India relations">India</a>, <a href="/wiki/Afghanistan%E2%80%93Japan_relations" title="Afghanistan–Japan relations">Japan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Kazakhstan" title="Foreign relations of Kazakhstan">Kazakhstan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Nepal" title="Foreign relations of Nepal">Nepal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Afghanistan%E2%80%93Russia_relations" title="Afghanistan–Russia relations">Russia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Afghanistan%E2%80%93South_Korea_relations" title="Afghanistan–South Korea relations">South Korea</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Afghanistan%E2%80%93United_Arab_Emirates_relations" title="Afghanistan–United Arab Emirates relations">UAE</a>, and so forth. The <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Foreign_Affairs_(Afghanistan)" title="Ministry of Foreign Affairs (Afghanistan)">Afghan Ministry of Foreign Affairs</a> continues to develop <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Afghanistan" title="Foreign relations of Afghanistan">diplomatic relations</a> with other countries around the world.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Assistance_Mission_in_Afghanistan" title="United Nations Assistance Mission in Afghanistan">United Nations Assistance Mission in Afghanistan</a> (UNAMA) was established in 2002 to help the country recover from decades of war.<sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194">&#91;194&#93;</a></sup> Today, several NATO member states deploy about 17,000 troops in Afghanistan as part of the <a href="/wiki/Resolute_Support_Mission" title="Resolute Support Mission">Resolute Support Mission</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-NATO_195-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NATO-195">&#91;195&#93;</a></sup> Its main purpose is to <a href="/wiki/NATO_Training_Mission-Afghanistan" title="NATO Training Mission-Afghanistan">train</a> the <a href="/wiki/Afghan_National_Security_Forces" title="Afghan National Security Forces">Afghan National Security Forces</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Afghan_Armed_Forces" title="Afghan Armed Forces">Afghan Armed Forces</a> are under the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Defense_(Afghanistan)" title="Ministry of Defense (Afghanistan)">Ministry of Defense</a>, which includes the <a href="/wiki/Afghan_Air_Force" title="Afghan Air Force">Afghan Air Force</a> (AAF) and the <a href="/wiki/Afghan_National_Army" title="Afghan National Army">Afghan National Army</a> (ANA). The <a href="/wiki/Afghan_Defense_University" class="mw-redirect" title="Afghan Defense University">Afghan Defense University</a> houses various educational establishments for the Afghan Armed Forces, including the <a href="/wiki/National_Military_Academy_of_Afghanistan" title="National Military Academy of Afghanistan">National Military Academy of Afghanistan</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196">&#91;196&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Law_enforcement">Law enforcement</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Law_enforcement_in_Afghanistan" title="Law enforcement in Afghanistan">Law enforcement in Afghanistan</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:ANP_trucks_in_Kunar.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/ANP_trucks_in_Kunar.jpg/220px-ANP_trucks_in_Kunar.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/ANP_trucks_in_Kunar.jpg/330px-ANP_trucks_in_Kunar.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/ANP_trucks_in_Kunar.jpg/440px-ANP_trucks_in_Kunar.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5616" data-file-height="3744" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:ANP_trucks_in_Kunar.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Afghan_National_Police" title="Afghan National Police">Afghan National Police</a> (ANP) in <a href="/wiki/Kunar_Province" title="Kunar Province">Kunar Province</a></div></div></div>
<p>Law enforcement in Afghanistan is the responsibility of the <a href="/wiki/Afghan_National_Police" title="Afghan National Police">Afghan National Police</a> (ANP), which is part of the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Interior_Affairs_(Afghanistan)" title="Ministry of Interior Affairs (Afghanistan)">Ministry of Interior Affairs</a>. The ANP consists of two primary branches, the Afghan Uniformed Police and the <a href="/wiki/Afghan_Border_Police" title="Afghan Border Police">Afghan Border Police</a>.  The mission of the Uniformed Police is to ensure security within Afghanistan, prevent crime, and protect property.  The Border Police is responsible for securing and maintaining the nation's borders with neighboring states as well as all international airports within the country.<sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197">&#91;197&#93;</a></sup>  Afghanistan's <a href="/wiki/Intelligence_agency" title="Intelligence agency">intelligence agency</a>, the <a href="/wiki/National_Directorate_of_Security" title="National Directorate of Security">National Directorate of Security</a> (NDS), assists the ANP with security matters.<sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198">&#91;198&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>All parts of Afghanistan are considered dangerous due to militant activities and terrorism-related incidents. Kidnapping for ransom and robberies are common in major cities. Every year hundreds of Afghan police are <a href="/wiki/List_of_Afghan_security_forces_fatality_reports_in_Afghanistan" title="List of Afghan security forces fatality reports in Afghanistan">killed</a> in the line of duty.<sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199">&#91;199&#93;</a></sup> Afghanistan is also the world's leading <a href="/wiki/Opium_production_in_Afghanistan" title="Opium production in Afghanistan">producer of opium</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200">&#91;200&#93;</a></sup> Afghanistan's <a href="/wiki/Opium_poppy" class="mw-redirect" title="Opium poppy">opium poppy</a> harvest produces more than 90% of illicit <a href="/wiki/Heroin" title="Heroin">heroin</a> globally, and more than 95% of the European supply.<sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201">&#91;201&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">&#91;202&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Counter_Narcotics_(Afghanistan)" title="Ministry of Counter Narcotics (Afghanistan)">Afghan Ministry of Counter Narcotics</a> is responsible for the monitoring and eradication of the illegal drug business.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Human_rights">Human rights</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Human_rights_in_Afghanistan" title="Human rights in Afghanistan">Human rights in Afghanistan</a> and <a href="/wiki/LGBT_rights_in_Afghanistan" title="LGBT rights in Afghanistan">LGBT rights in Afghanistan</a></div>
<p>Journalist in Afghanistan face threat from both the security forces and insurgents.<sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203">&#91;203&#93;</a></sup> Afghan Journalists Safety Committee (AJSC) in 2017 claim that Afghan government accounted for 46% of the attacks on Afghans journalist, while insurgents were responsible for rest of the attacks.<sup id="cite_ref-204" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-204">&#91;204&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Homosexuality is illegal and is a <a href="/wiki/Death_penalty_for_homosexuality" title="Death penalty for homosexuality">capital offense</a> in Afghanistan.<sup id="cite_ref-205" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-205">&#91;205&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Afghanistan" title="Economy of Afghanistan">Economy of Afghanistan</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Afghan_pomegranate_processing.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Afghan_pomegranate_processing.jpg/220px-Afghan_pomegranate_processing.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Afghan_pomegranate_processing.jpg/330px-Afghan_pomegranate_processing.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Afghan_pomegranate_processing.jpg/440px-Afghan_pomegranate_processing.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2000" data-file-height="1500" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Afghan_pomegranate_processing.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Workers processing <a href="/wiki/Pomegranate_production_in_Afghanistan" title="Pomegranate production in Afghanistan">pomegranates</a> (<i>anaar</i>), which Afghanistan is famous for in Asia</div></div></div>
<p>Afghanistan's nominal <a href="/wiki/Gross_domestic_product" title="Gross domestic product">GDP</a> was $21.7 billion in 2018, or $72.9 billion by <a href="/wiki/Purchasing_power_parity" title="Purchasing power parity">purchasing power parity</a> (PPP).<sup id="cite_ref-imf2_7-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-imf2-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> Its <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(PPP)_per_capita" title="List of countries by GDP (PPP) per capita">GDP per capita</a> is $2,024 (PPP).<sup id="cite_ref-imf2_7-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-imf2-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> Despite having $1 trillion or more in mineral deposits,<sup id="cite_ref-206" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-206">&#91;206&#93;</a></sup> it remains one of the world's <a href="/wiki/Least_developed_countries" class="mw-redirect" title="Least developed countries">least developed countries</a>. The country imports over $7 billion worth of goods but exports only $784 million, mainly <a href="/wiki/Fruit" title="Fruit">fruits</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nut_(fruit)" title="Nut (fruit)">nuts</a>. It has $2.8 billion in <a href="/wiki/External_debt" title="External debt">external debt</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Factbook_5-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Factbook-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Agricultural production is the backbone of Afghanistan's economy.<sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207">&#91;207&#93;</a></sup> The country is known for producing <a href="/wiki/Pomegranate_production_in_Afghanistan" title="Pomegranate production in Afghanistan">pomegranates</a>, grapes, apricots, melons, and several other fresh and dry fruits. It is also known as the world's largest producer of <a href="/wiki/Opium_production_in_Afghanistan" title="Opium production in Afghanistan">opium</a>. As much as 16% or more of the nation's economy is derived from the cultivation and sale of opium.<sup id="cite_ref-208" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-208">&#91;208&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Afghan_women_at_a_textile_factory_in_Kabul.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Afghan_women_at_a_textile_factory_in_Kabul.jpg/220px-Afghan_women_at_a_textile_factory_in_Kabul.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="137" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Afghan_women_at_a_textile_factory_in_Kabul.jpg/330px-Afghan_women_at_a_textile_factory_in_Kabul.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Afghan_women_at_a_textile_factory_in_Kabul.jpg/440px-Afghan_women_at_a_textile_factory_in_Kabul.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3022" data-file-height="1877" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Afghan_women_at_a_textile_factory_in_Kabul.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Afghan women at a textile factory in Kabul</div></div></div>
<p>While the nation's current account deficit is largely financed with donor money, only a small portion is provided directly to the government budget. The rest is provided to non-budgetary expenditure and donor-designated projects through the United Nations system and non-governmental organizations.<sup id="cite_ref-209" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-209">&#91;209&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Afghanistan,_Trends_in_the_Human_Development_Index_1970-2010.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Afghanistan%2C_Trends_in_the_Human_Development_Index_1970-2010.png/220px-Afghanistan%2C_Trends_in_the_Human_Development_Index_1970-2010.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="127" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Afghanistan%2C_Trends_in_the_Human_Development_Index_1970-2010.png/330px-Afghanistan%2C_Trends_in_the_Human_Development_Index_1970-2010.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Afghanistan%2C_Trends_in_the_Human_Development_Index_1970-2010.png/440px-Afghanistan%2C_Trends_in_the_Human_Development_Index_1970-2010.png 2x" data-file-width="443" data-file-height="255" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Afghanistan,_Trends_in_the_Human_Development_Index_1970-2010.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Afghanistan, Trends in the <a href="/wiki/Human_Development_Index" title="Human Development Index">Human Development Index</a>, 1970–2010</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Da_Afghanistan_Bank" title="Da Afghanistan Bank">Da Afghanistan Bank</a> serves as the central bank of the nation<sup id="cite_ref-210" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-210">&#91;210&#93;</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Afghan_afghani" title="Afghan afghani">"Afghani"</a> (AFN) is the national currency, with an exchange rate of about 75 Afghanis to <a href="/wiki/United_States_dollar" title="United States dollar">1 US dollar</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-211" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-211">&#91;211&#93;</a></sup> A number of local and foreign banks operate in the country, including the <a href="/wiki/Afghanistan_International_Bank" title="Afghanistan International Bank">Afghanistan International Bank</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_Kabul_Bank" title="New Kabul Bank">New Kabul Bank</a>, <a href="/wiki/Azizi_Bank" title="Azizi Bank">Azizi Bank</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pashtany_Bank" title="Pashtany Bank">Pashtany Bank</a>, <a href="/wiki/Standard_Chartered_Bank" class="mw-redirect" title="Standard Chartered Bank">Standard Chartered Bank</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/First_MicroFinance_Bank-Afghanistan" class="mw-redirect" title="First MicroFinance Bank-Afghanistan">First Micro Finance Bank</a>.
</p><p>One of the main drivers for the current economic recovery is the return of over 5 million <a href="/wiki/Afghan_diaspora" title="Afghan diaspora">expatriates</a>, who brought with them entrepreneurship and wealth-creating skills as well as much needed funds to start up businesses. Many Afghans are now involved in construction, which is one of the largest industries in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-212" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-212">&#91;212&#93;</a></sup> Some of the major national construction projects include the <span class="nowrap">$35 billion</span> New Kabul City next to the capital, the Aino Mena project in Kandahar, and the <a href="/wiki/Ghazi_Amanullah_Khan_Town" class="mw-redirect" title="Ghazi Amanullah Khan Town">Ghazi Amanullah Khan Town</a> near Jalalabad.<sup id="cite_ref-213" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-213">&#91;213&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-214" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-214">&#91;214&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-215" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-215">&#91;215&#93;</a></sup> Similar development projects have also begun in <a href="/wiki/Herat" title="Herat">Herat</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mazar-e-Sharif" class="mw-redirect" title="Mazar-e-Sharif">Mazar-e-Sharif</a>, and other cities.<sup id="cite_ref-216" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-216">&#91;216&#93;</a></sup> An estimated 400,000 people enter the labor market each year.<sup id="cite_ref-217" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-217">&#91;217&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Afghan_market_teeming_with_vendors_and_shoppers_2-4-09.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Afghan_market_teeming_with_vendors_and_shoppers_2-4-09.jpg/200px-Afghan_market_teeming_with_vendors_and_shoppers_2-4-09.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="129" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Afghan_market_teeming_with_vendors_and_shoppers_2-4-09.jpg/300px-Afghan_market_teeming_with_vendors_and_shoppers_2-4-09.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Afghan_market_teeming_with_vendors_and_shoppers_2-4-09.jpg/400px-Afghan_market_teeming_with_vendors_and_shoppers_2-4-09.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3015" data-file-height="1948" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Afghan_market_teeming_with_vendors_and_shoppers_2-4-09.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A bustling market street in central Kabul, 2009</div></div></div>
<p>Several small companies and factories began operating in different parts of the country, which not only provide revenues to the government but also create new jobs. Improvements to the business environment have resulted in more than $1.5 billion in <a href="/wiki/Telecommunication" title="Telecommunication">telecom</a> investment and created more than 100,000 jobs since 2003.<sup id="cite_ref-218" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-218">&#91;218&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Afghan_rug" title="Afghan rug">Afghan rugs</a> are becoming popular again, allowing many carpet dealers around the country to hire more workers.
</p><p>Afghanistan is a member of <a href="/wiki/World_Trade_Organization" title="World Trade Organization">WTO</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_Asian_Association_for_Regional_Cooperation" title="South Asian Association for Regional Cooperation">SAARC</a>, <a href="/wiki/Economic_Cooperation_Organization" title="Economic Cooperation Organization">ECO</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_the_OIC" class="mw-redirect" title="Economy of the OIC">OIC</a>. It holds an observer status in <a href="/wiki/Shanghai_Cooperation_Organisation" title="Shanghai Cooperation Organisation">SCO</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mining">Mining</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Mining_in_Afghanistan" title="Mining in Afghanistan">Mining in Afghanistan</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Lapis_Lazuli_from_Afganistan.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Lapis_Lazuli_from_Afganistan.jpg/200px-Lapis_Lazuli_from_Afganistan.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="268" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Lapis_Lazuli_from_Afganistan.jpg/300px-Lapis_Lazuli_from_Afganistan.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Lapis_Lazuli_from_Afganistan.jpg/400px-Lapis_Lazuli_from_Afganistan.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1936" data-file-height="2592" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Lapis_Lazuli_from_Afganistan.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Lapis_lazuli" title="Lapis lazuli">Lapis lazuli</a> stones</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Michael_E._O%27Hanlon" title="Michael E. O&#39;Hanlon">Michael E. O'Hanlon</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Brookings_Institution" title="Brookings Institution">Brookings Institution</a> estimated that if Afghanistan generates about $10 billion per year from its <a href="/wiki/Mining_in_Afghanistan" title="Mining in Afghanistan">mineral deposits</a>, its <a href="/wiki/Gross_national_product" class="mw-redirect" title="Gross national product">gross national product</a> would double and provide long-term funding for Afghan security forces and other critical needs.<sup id="cite_ref-219" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-219">&#91;219&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/United_States_Geological_Survey" title="United States Geological Survey">United States Geological Survey</a> (USGS) estimated in 2006 that northern Afghanistan has an average 460&#160;million&#160;m<sup>3</sup> (2.9&#160;billion&#160;bbl) of <a href="/wiki/Crude_oil" class="mw-redirect" title="Crude oil">crude oil</a>, 440&#160;billion&#160;m<sup>3</sup> (15.7&#160;trillion&#160;cu&#160;ft) of natural gas, and 67&#160;billion&#160;L (562&#160;million&#160;US&#160;bbl) of <a href="/wiki/Natural_gas_liquids" class="mw-redirect" title="Natural gas liquids">natural gas liquids</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-klett2006_220-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-klett2006-220">&#91;220&#93;</a></sup> In 2011, Afghanistan signed an oil exploration contract with <a href="/wiki/China_National_Petroleum_Corporation" title="China National Petroleum Corporation">China National Petroleum Corporation</a> (CNPC) for the development of three oil fields along the Amu Darya river in the north.<sup id="cite_ref-221" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-221">&#91;221&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The country has significant amounts of <a href="/wiki/Lithium" title="Lithium">lithium</a>, copper, gold, coal, <a href="/wiki/Iron_ore" title="Iron ore">iron ore</a>, and other <a href="/wiki/Minerals" class="mw-redirect" title="Minerals">minerals</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-peters2007_154-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-peters2007-154">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-bgs_155-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bgs-155">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Afghanistan&#39;s_Mineral_Fortune_222-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Afghanistan&#39;s_Mineral_Fortune-222">&#91;222&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Khanashin" title="Khanashin">Khanashin</a> <a href="/wiki/Carbonatite" title="Carbonatite">carbonatite</a> in <a href="/wiki/Helmand_Province" title="Helmand Province">Helmand Province</a> contains 1,000,000 tonnes (980,000 <a href="/wiki/Long_ton" title="Long ton">long tons</a>; 1,100,000 <a href="/wiki/Short_ton" title="Short ton">short tons</a>) of <a href="/wiki/Rare_earth_element" class="mw-redirect" title="Rare earth element">rare earth elements</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-tucker2011_223-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tucker2011-223">&#91;223&#93;</a></sup> In 2007, a 30-year lease was granted for the <a href="/wiki/Mes_Aynak#Copper_Mine" title="Mes Aynak">Aynak</a> copper mine to the <a href="/wiki/China_Metallurgical_Group" class="mw-redirect" title="China Metallurgical Group">China Metallurgical Group</a> for $3 billion,<sup id="cite_ref-224" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-224">&#91;224&#93;</a></sup> making it the biggest foreign investment and private business venture in Afghanistan's history.<sup id="cite_ref-225" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-225">&#91;225&#93;</a></sup> The state-run <a href="/wiki/Steel_Authority_of_India" title="Steel Authority of India">Steel Authority of India</a> won the mining rights to develop the huge <a href="/wiki/Hajigak_Pass" title="Hajigak Pass">Hajigak</a> iron ore deposit in central Afghanistan.<sup id="cite_ref-226" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-226">&#91;226&#93;</a></sup> Government officials estimate that 30% of the country's untapped mineral deposits are worth at least <span class="nowrap">$1 trillion</span>.<sup id="cite_ref-bbcminerals_156-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbcminerals-156">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup> One official asserted that "this will become the backbone of the Afghan economy" and a Pentagon memo stated that Afghanistan could become the "Saudi Arabia of lithium".<sup id="cite_ref-risen2010_227-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-risen2010-227">&#91;227&#93;</a></sup> In a 2011 news story, the <i><a href="/wiki/The_Christian_Science_Monitor" title="The Christian Science Monitor">CSM</a></i> reported, "The United States and other Western nations that have borne the brunt of the cost of the Afghan war have been conspicuously absent from the bidding process on Afghanistan's mineral deposits, leaving it mostly to regional powers."<sup id="cite_ref-228" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-228">&#91;228&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation">Transportation</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Afghanistan" title="Transport in Afghanistan">Transport in Afghanistan</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Air">Air</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_airports_in_Afghanistan" title="List of airports in Afghanistan">List of airports in Afghanistan</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ariana_Afghan_A310-300_F-GEMO.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Ariana_Afghan_A310-300_F-GEMO.jpg/220px-Ariana_Afghan_A310-300_F-GEMO.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="139" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Ariana_Afghan_A310-300_F-GEMO.jpg/330px-Ariana_Afghan_A310-300_F-GEMO.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Ariana_Afghan_A310-300_F-GEMO.jpg/440px-Ariana_Afghan_A310-300_F-GEMO.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1214" data-file-height="768" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ariana_Afghan_A310-300_F-GEMO.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>An <a href="/wiki/Ariana_Afghan_Airlines" title="Ariana Afghan Airlines">Ariana Afghan Airlines</a> <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A310" title="Airbus A310">Airbus A310</a> in 2006</div></div></div>
<p>Air transport in Afghanistan is provided by the national carrier, <a href="/wiki/Ariana_Afghan_Airlines" title="Ariana Afghan Airlines">Ariana Afghan Airlines</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-EU_To_Impose_Ban_On_Afghan_Planes_229-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EU_To_Impose_Ban_On_Afghan_Planes-229">&#91;229&#93;</a></sup> and by the private company <a href="/wiki/Kam_Air" title="Kam Air">Kam Air</a>. Airlines from a number of countries also provide flights in and out of the country. These include <a href="/wiki/Air_India" title="Air India">Air India</a>, <a href="/wiki/Emirates_(airline)" title="Emirates (airline)">Emirates</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gulf_Air" title="Gulf Air">Gulf Air</a>, <a href="/wiki/Iran_Aseman_Airlines" title="Iran Aseman Airlines">Iran Aseman Airlines</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pakistan_International_Airlines" title="Pakistan International Airlines">Pakistan International Airlines</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Turkish_Airlines" title="Turkish Airlines">Turkish Airlines</a>.
</p><p>The country has four international airports: <a href="/wiki/Hamid_Karzai_International_Airport" title="Hamid Karzai International Airport">Hamid Karzai International Airport</a> (formerly Kabul International Airport), <a href="/wiki/Kandahar_International_Airport" title="Kandahar International Airport">Kandahar International Airport</a>, <a href="/wiki/Herat_International_Airport" title="Herat International Airport">Herat International Airport</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Mazar-e_Sharif_International_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Mazar-e Sharif International Airport">Mazar-e Sharif International Airport</a>. Including domestic airports, there are 43.<sup id="cite_ref-Factbook_5-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Factbook-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rail">Rail</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Rail_transport_in_Afghanistan" title="Rail transport in Afghanistan">Rail transport in Afghanistan</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Rail_crossing_in_northern_Afghanistan.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Rail_crossing_in_northern_Afghanistan.jpg/250px-Rail_crossing_in_northern_Afghanistan.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="142" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Rail_crossing_in_northern_Afghanistan.jpg/375px-Rail_crossing_in_northern_Afghanistan.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Rail_crossing_in_northern_Afghanistan.jpg/500px-Rail_crossing_in_northern_Afghanistan.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4240" data-file-height="2400" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Rail_crossing_in_northern_Afghanistan.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Rail crossing in northern Afghanistan on the line towards Uzbekistan</div></div></div>
<p>The country has three rail links: one, a 75-kilometer (47&#160;mi) line from <a href="/wiki/Mazar-i-Sharif" title="Mazar-i-Sharif">Mazar-i-Sharif</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Afghanistan%E2%80%93Uzbekistan_Friendship_Bridge" title="Afghanistan–Uzbekistan Friendship Bridge">Uzbekistan border</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-230" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-230">&#91;230&#93;</a></sup> a 10-kilometer (6.2&#160;mi) long line from <a href="/wiki/Toraghundi" class="mw-redirect" title="Toraghundi">Toraghundi</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Turkmenistan" title="Turkmenistan">Turkmenistan</a> border (where it continues as part of <a href="/wiki/T%C3%BCrkmendemir%C3%BDollary" title="Türkmendemirýollary">Turkmen Railways</a>); and a short link from <a href="/wiki/Aqina" title="Aqina">Aqina</a> across the Turkmen border to <a href="/wiki/Kerki" title="Kerki">Kerki</a>, which is planned to be extended further across Afghanistan.<sup id="cite_ref-231" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-231">&#91;231&#93;</a></sup> These lines are used for freight only and there is no passenger service. A rail line between <a href="/wiki/Khaf,_Iran" title="Khaf, Iran">Khaf</a>, Iran and <a href="/wiki/Herat" title="Herat">Herat</a>, western Afghanistan, intended for both freight and passengers, is under construction as of 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-232" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-232">&#91;232&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-233" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-233">&#91;233&#93;</a></sup> About 125 kilometers (78&#160;mi) of the line will lie on the Afghan side.<sup id="cite_ref-234" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-234">&#91;234&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-235" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-235">&#91;235&#93;</a></sup> There are various proposals for the construction of additional rail lines in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-236" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-236">&#91;236&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Roads">Roads</span></h3>
<p>The most important road in Afghanistan is <a href="/wiki/Highway_1_(Afghanistan)" title="Highway 1 (Afghanistan)">Highway 1</a>, also called the Ring Road, which extends for 2,210 kilometers (1,370&#160;mi) and connects four major cities: Kabul, Ghazni, Kandahar, and Herat.<sup id="cite_ref-237" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-237">&#91;237&#93;</a></sup>  A key portion of Highway 1 is the <a href="/wiki/Salang_Tunnel" title="Salang Tunnel">Salang Tunnel</a>, completed in 1964, which facilitates travel through the Hindu Kush mountain range and connects northern and southern Afghanistan.<sup id="cite_ref-238" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-238">&#91;238&#93;</a></sup> Traveling by bus in Afghanistan remains dangerous due to militant activities.<sup id="cite_ref-239" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-239">&#91;239&#93;</a></sup> Serious traffic accidents are common on Afghan roads and highways, particularly on the <a href="/wiki/Kabul%E2%80%93Kandahar_Highway" title="Kabul–Kandahar Highway">Kabul–Kandahar</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Kabul%E2%80%93Jalalabad_Road" title="Kabul–Jalalabad Road">Kabul–Jalalabad Road</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-240" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-240">&#91;240&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Health">Health</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Health_in_Afghanistan" title="Health in Afghanistan">Health in Afghanistan</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Kabul_Military_Hospital_-_panoramio.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Kabul_Military_Hospital_-_panoramio.jpg/220px-Kabul_Military_Hospital_-_panoramio.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Kabul_Military_Hospital_-_panoramio.jpg/330px-Kabul_Military_Hospital_-_panoramio.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Kabul_Military_Hospital_-_panoramio.jpg/440px-Kabul_Military_Hospital_-_panoramio.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="686" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Kabul_Military_Hospital_-_panoramio.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A hospital in Kabul</div></div></div>
<p>According to the <a href="/wiki/Human_Development_Index" title="Human Development Index">Human Development Index</a>, Afghanistan is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_Human_Development_Index" title="List of countries by Human Development Index">15th least developed country in the world</a>. The average <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_life_expectancy" title="List of countries by life expectancy">life expectancy</a> is estimated to be around 60 years.<sup id="cite_ref-WHO_241-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WHO-241">&#91;241&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-uis.unesco.org_242-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-uis.unesco.org-242">&#91;242&#93;</a></sup> The country's <a href="/wiki/Maternal_mortality" class="mw-redirect" title="Maternal mortality">maternal mortality</a> rate is 396 deaths/100,000 live births and its <a href="/wiki/Infant_mortality" title="Infant mortality">infant mortality</a> rate is 66<sup id="cite_ref-uis.unesco.org_242-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-uis.unesco.org-242">&#91;242&#93;</a></sup> to 112.8 deaths in every 1,000 live births.<sup id="cite_ref-Factbook_5-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Factbook-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Public_Health_(Afghanistan)" title="Ministry of Public Health (Afghanistan)">Ministry of Public Health</a> plans to cut the infant mortality rate to 400 for every 100,000 live births before 2020. The country has more than 3,000 <a href="/wiki/Midwifery" title="Midwifery">midwives</a>, with an additional 300 to 400 being trained each year.<sup id="cite_ref-csm_243-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-csm-243">&#91;243&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>There are over 100 <a href="/wiki/List_of_hospitals_in_Afghanistan" title="List of hospitals in Afghanistan">hospitals in Afghanistan</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-244" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-244">&#91;244&#93;</a></sup> with the most advanced treatments being available in Kabul. The <a href="/wiki/French_Medical_Institute_for_Children" title="French Medical Institute for Children">French Medical Institute for Children</a> and <a href="/wiki/Indira_Gandhi_Children%27s_Hospital" title="Indira Gandhi Children&#39;s Hospital">Indira Gandhi Children's Hospital</a> in Kabul are the leading <a href="/wiki/Children%27s_hospital" title="Children&#39;s hospital">children's hospitals</a> in the country. Some of the other leading hospitals in Kabul include the <a href="/wiki/Jamhuriat_Hospital" title="Jamhuriat Hospital">Jamhuriat Hospital</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jinnah_Hospital_(Kabul)" class="mw-redirect" title="Jinnah Hospital (Kabul)">Jinnah Hospital</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-245" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-245">&#91;245&#93;</a></sup> In spite of all this, many Afghans travel to Pakistan and India for advanced treatment.
</p><p>It was reported in 2006 that nearly 60% of the Afghan population lives within a two-hour walk of the nearest health facility.<sup id="cite_ref-USAID-Health_246-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USAID-Health-246">&#91;246&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Disability" title="Disability">Disability</a> rate is also high in Afghanistan due to the decades of war.<sup id="cite_ref-247" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-247">&#91;247&#93;</a></sup> It was reported recently that about 80,000 people are missing limbs.<sup id="cite_ref-248" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-248">&#91;248&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-249" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-249">&#91;249&#93;</a></sup> Non-governmental charities such as <a href="/wiki/Save_the_Children" title="Save the Children">Save the Children</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mahboba%27s_Promise" title="Mahboba&#39;s Promise">Mahboba's Promise</a> assist orphans in association with governmental structures.<sup id="cite_ref-250" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-250">&#91;250&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Demographic_and_Health_Surveys" title="Demographic and Health Surveys">Demographic and Health Surveys</a> is working with the <a href="/wiki/Indian_Institute_of_Health_Management_Research" title="Indian Institute of Health Management Research">Indian Institute of Health Management Research</a> and others to conduct a survey in Afghanistan focusing on <a href="/wiki/Maternal_death" title="Maternal death">maternal death</a>, among other things.<sup id="cite_ref-MEASUREDHS_251-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MEASUREDHS-251">&#91;251&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Afghanistan" title="Education in Afghanistan">Education in Afghanistan</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:UNESCO_Institute_of_Statistics_Afghanistan_Literacy_Rate_population_plus15_1980-2015.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/UNESCO_Institute_of_Statistics_Afghanistan_Literacy_Rate_population_plus15_1980-2015.png/220px-UNESCO_Institute_of_Statistics_Afghanistan_Literacy_Rate_population_plus15_1980-2015.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="177" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/UNESCO_Institute_of_Statistics_Afghanistan_Literacy_Rate_population_plus15_1980-2015.png/330px-UNESCO_Institute_of_Statistics_Afghanistan_Literacy_Rate_population_plus15_1980-2015.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/f8/UNESCO_Institute_of_Statistics_Afghanistan_Literacy_Rate_population_plus15_1980-2015.png 2x" data-file-width="407" data-file-height="328" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:UNESCO_Institute_of_Statistics_Afghanistan_Literacy_Rate_population_plus15_1980-2015.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>UNESCO Institute of Statistics Afghanistan Literacy Rate population plus15 1980–2015</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Education_in_Afghanistan" title="Education in Afghanistan">Education in Afghanistan</a> includes <a href="/wiki/K%E2%80%9312_(education)" class="mw-redirect" title="K–12 (education)">K–12</a> and <a href="/wiki/Higher_education" title="Higher education">higher education</a>, which is overseen by the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Education_(Afghanistan)" title="Ministry of Education (Afghanistan)">Ministry of Education</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Higher_Education_(Afghanistan)" title="Ministry of Higher Education (Afghanistan)">Ministry of Higher Education</a>. There are over 16,000 schools in the country and roughly 9 million students. Of this, about 60% are males and 40% females. Over 174,000 students are enrolled in different <a href="/wiki/List_of_universities_in_Afghanistan" title="List of universities in Afghanistan">universities</a> around the country. About 21% of these are females.<sup id="cite_ref-USAID-Education_252-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USAID-Education-252">&#91;252&#93;</a></sup> Former Education Minister <a href="/wiki/Ghulam_Farooq_Wardak" title="Ghulam Farooq Wardak">Ghulam Farooq Wardak</a> had stated that construction of 8,000 schools is required for the remaining children who are deprived of <a href="/wiki/Formal_learning" title="Formal learning">formal learning</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Wardak_seeks_$3b_in_aid_for_school_buildings_253-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wardak_seeks_$3b_in_aid_for_school_buildings-253">&#91;253&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The top universities in Afghanistan are the <a href="/wiki/American_University_of_Afghanistan" title="American University of Afghanistan">American University of Afghanistan</a> (AUAF) followed by <a href="/wiki/Kabul_University" title="Kabul University">Kabul University</a> (KU), both of which are located in Kabul. The <a href="/wiki/National_Military_Academy_of_Afghanistan" title="National Military Academy of Afghanistan">National Military Academy of Afghanistan</a>, modeled after the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Military_Academy" title="United States Military Academy">United States Military Academy</a> at West Point, is a four-year military development institution dedicated to graduating officers for the <a href="/wiki/Afghan_Armed_Forces" title="Afghan Armed Forces">Afghan Armed Forces</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Afghan_Defense_University" class="mw-redirect" title="Afghan Defense University">Afghan Defense University</a> was constructed near <a href="/wiki/Qargha_Reservoir" title="Qargha Reservoir">Qargha</a> in Kabul. Major universities outside of Kabul include <a href="/wiki/Kandahar_University" title="Kandahar University">Kandahar University</a> in the south, <a href="/wiki/Herat_University" title="Herat University">Herat University</a> in the northwest, <a href="/wiki/Balkh_University" title="Balkh University">Balkh University</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kunduz_University" title="Kunduz University">Kunduz University</a> in the north, <a href="/wiki/Nangarhar_University" title="Nangarhar University">Nangarhar University</a> and <a href="/wiki/Khost_University" class="mw-redirect" title="Khost University">Khost University</a> in the east. The United States is building six faculties of education and five provincial teacher training colleges around the country, two large secondary schools in Kabul, and one school in Jalalabad.<sup id="cite_ref-USAID-Education_252-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USAID-Education-252">&#91;252&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The literacy rate of the population is 38.2% (males 52% and females 24.2%).<sup id="cite_ref-Factbook_5-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Factbook-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> The Afghan National Security Forces are provided with mandatory literacy courses.<sup id="cite_ref-autogeneratedmil_254-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogeneratedmil-254">&#91;254&#93;</a></sup> 
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Afghanistan" title="Culture of Afghanistan">Culture of Afghanistan</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Grupka_Pasztun%C3%B3w_-_Qajs%C4%81r_-_001620s.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Grupka_Pasztun%C3%B3w_-_Qajs%C4%81r_-_001620s.jpg/250px-Grupka_Pasztun%C3%B3w_-_Qajs%C4%81r_-_001620s.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="168" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Grupka_Pasztun%C3%B3w_-_Qajs%C4%81r_-_001620s.jpg/375px-Grupka_Pasztun%C3%B3w_-_Qajs%C4%81r_-_001620s.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Grupka_Pasztun%C3%B3w_-_Qajs%C4%81r_-_001620s.jpg/500px-Grupka_Pasztun%C3%B3w_-_Qajs%C4%81r_-_001620s.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1920" data-file-height="1293" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Grupka_Pasztun%C3%B3w_-_Qajs%C4%81r_-_001620s.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Men wearing traditional <a href="/wiki/Pashtun_dress" class="mw-redirect" title="Pashtun dress">Afghan (Pashtun) dress</a> in <a href="/wiki/Faryab_Province" title="Faryab Province">Faryab Province</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Afghan_girls_in_traditional_clothes-May_2011.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Afghan_girls_in_traditional_clothes-May_2011.jpg/200px-Afghan_girls_in_traditional_clothes-May_2011.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="133" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Afghan_girls_in_traditional_clothes-May_2011.jpg/300px-Afghan_girls_in_traditional_clothes-May_2011.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Afghan_girls_in_traditional_clothes-May_2011.jpg/400px-Afghan_girls_in_traditional_clothes-May_2011.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4256" data-file-height="2832" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Afghan_girls_in_traditional_clothes-May_2011.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Ethnic <a href="/wiki/Tajiks" title="Tajiks">Tajik</a> girls in traditional clothing in <a href="/wiki/Mazar-i-Sharif" title="Mazar-i-Sharif">Mazar-i-Sharif</a></div></div></div>
<p>Afghanistan is a predominantly tribal society, with different regions of the country having their own cultures.  In the southern and eastern region, the people live according to the <a href="/wiki/Pashtun_culture" title="Pashtun culture">Pashtun culture</a> by following <a href="/wiki/Pashtunwali" title="Pashtunwali">Pashtunwali</a> (the Pashtun way).<sup id="cite_ref-255" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-255">&#91;255&#93;</a></sup> Key tenets of Pashtunwali include <a href="/wiki/Melmastia" title="Melmastia">hospitality</a>, the provision of <a href="/wiki/Nanawatai" title="Nanawatai">sanctuary</a> to those seeking refuge, and revenge for the shedding of blood.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDupree1997126_256-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDupree1997126-256">&#91;256&#93;</a></sup> The Pashtuns (and Baloch) are largely connected to the culture of South Asia. The remaining Afghans are culturally <a href="/wiki/Persianization" title="Persianization">Persian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Turkic_peoples" title="Turkic peoples">Turkic</a>. Some non-Pashtuns who live in proximity with Pashtuns have adopted Pashtunwali in a process called <a href="/wiki/Pashtunization" title="Pashtunization">Pashtunization</a>, while some Pashtuns have been <a href="/wiki/Persianization" title="Persianization">Persianized</a>. Those who have lived in Pakistan and Iran over the last 30 years have been further influenced by the cultures of those neighboring nations.
</p><p>Afghans, particularly Pashtuns, are noted for their tribal solidarity and high regard for personal honor.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBarfield201259_257-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBarfield201259-257">&#91;257&#93;</a></sup> One writer considers the tribal system to be the best way of organizing large groups of people in a country that is geographically difficult, and in a society that, from a materialistic point of view, has an uncomplicated lifestyle.<sup id="cite_ref-Heathcote_258-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Heathcote-258">&#91;258&#93;</a></sup> There are various <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_groups_in_Afghanistan" title="Ethnic groups in Afghanistan">Afghan tribes</a>, and an estimated 2–3 million <a href="/wiki/Kochi_people" title="Kochi people">nomads</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-259" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-259">&#91;259&#93;</a></sup> Afghan culture is deeply <a href="/wiki/Islamic_culture" title="Islamic culture">Islamic</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBarfield201240-41_260-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBarfield201240-41-260">&#91;260&#93;</a></sup> but pre-Islamic practices persist.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDupree1997104_261-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDupree1997104-261">&#91;261&#93;</a></sup>  One example is <i><a href="/wiki/Bacha_bazi" title="Bacha bazi">bacha bazi</a></i>, a term for activities involving sexual relations between older men and younger adolescent men, or boys.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC_Rustam_Qobil_262-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_Rustam_Qobil-262">&#91;262&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The nation has a complex history that has survived either in its current cultures or in the form of various languages and monuments. However, many of its historic monuments have been damaged in modern times.<sup id="cite_ref-263" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-263">&#91;263&#93;</a></sup> The two famous <a href="/wiki/Buddhas_of_Bamiyan" class="mw-redirect" title="Buddhas of Bamiyan">Buddhas of Bamiyan</a> were destroyed by the Taliban, who regarded them as <a href="/wiki/Idolatry" title="Idolatry">idolatrous</a>. Despite that, archaeologists are still finding Buddhist relics in different parts of the country, some of them dating back to the 2nd century.<sup id="cite_ref-264" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-264">&#91;264&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-265" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-265">&#91;265&#93;</a></sup> This indicates that Buddhism was widespread in Afghanistan. Other historical places include the cities of <a href="/wiki/Herat" title="Herat">Herat</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kandahar" title="Kandahar">Kandahar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ghazni" title="Ghazni">Ghazni</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mazar-i-Sharif" title="Mazar-i-Sharif">Mazar-i-Sharif</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Zaranj" title="Zaranj">Zaranj</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Minaret_of_Jam" title="Minaret of Jam">Minaret of Jam</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Hari_River,_Afghanistan" class="mw-redirect" title="Hari River, Afghanistan">Hari River</a> valley is a <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">UNESCO World Heritage site</a>. A cloak reputedly worn by Islam's prophet <a href="/wiki/Muhammad" title="Muhammad">Muhammad</a> is kept inside the <a href="/wiki/Shrine_of_the_Cloak" title="Shrine of the Cloak">Shrine of the Cloak</a> in Kandahar, a city founded by <a href="/wiki/Alexander_the_Great" title="Alexander the Great">Alexander</a> and the first capital of Afghanistan. The <a href="/wiki/Citadel_of_Herat" class="mw-redirect" title="Citadel of Herat">citadel of Alexander</a> in the western city of Herat has been renovated in recent years and is a popular attraction for tourists. In the north of the country is the <a href="/wiki/Shrine_of_Ali" class="mw-redirect" title="Shrine of Ali">Shrine of Ali</a>, believed by many to be the location where <a href="/wiki/Ali" title="Ali">Ali</a> was buried.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDupree1997115_266-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDupree1997115-266">&#91;266&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/National_Museum_of_Afghanistan" title="National Museum of Afghanistan">National Museum of Afghanistan</a> is located in Kabul.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Women">Women</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Women_in_Afghanistan" title="Women in Afghanistan">Women in Afghanistan</a></div>
<p>According to <a href="/wiki/Global_Rights" title="Global Rights">Global Rights</a>, almost 90% of women in Afghanistan experience physical abuse, sexual abuse, psychological abuse or forced marriage. The perpetrators of these crimes are the families of the victim.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_267-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-267">&#91;267&#93;</a></sup> A 2009 proposal for a law against the violence of women could only be passed through a presidential decree.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_267-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-267">&#91;267&#93;</a></sup> 
</p><p>In 2012, Afghanistan recorded 240 cases of <a href="/wiki/Honor_killing" title="Honor killing">honor killing</a>, but the total number is believed to be much higher. Of the reported honor killings, 21% were committed by the victims’ husbands, 7% by their brothers, 4% by their fathers, and the rest by other relatives.<sup id="cite_ref-268" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-268">&#91;268&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-269" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-269">&#91;269&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Child_marriage_in_Afghanistan" title="Child marriage in Afghanistan">Child marriage</a> is prevalent in Afghanistan.<sup id="cite_ref-Medica_Mondiale_270-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Medica_Mondiale-270">&#91;270&#93;</a></sup> The legal age for marriage is 16.<sup id="cite_ref-271" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-271">&#91;271&#93;</a></sup>  The most preferred marriage in Afghan society is to one's <a href="/wiki/Parallel_and_cross_cousins" title="Parallel and cross cousins">parallel cousin</a>, and the groom is often expected to pay a <a href="/wiki/Bride_price" title="Bride price">bride price</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDupree1997122,_198_272-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDupree1997122,_198-272">&#91;272&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media_and_entertainment">Media and entertainment</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Media_of_Afghanistan" title="Media of Afghanistan">Media of Afghanistan</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:TOLOnews_Studio_.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/TOLOnews_Studio_.jpg/220px-TOLOnews_Studio_.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/TOLOnews_Studio_.jpg/330px-TOLOnews_Studio_.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/TOLOnews_Studio_.jpg/440px-TOLOnews_Studio_.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4608" data-file-height="2592" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:TOLOnews_Studio_.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Studio of <a href="/wiki/TOLOnews" title="TOLOnews">TOLOnews</a> in Kabul</div></div></div>
<p>Afghanistan has around 350 <a href="/wiki/List_of_radio_stations_in_Afghanistan" title="List of radio stations in Afghanistan">radio stations</a> and over 200 television stations.<sup id="cite_ref-TOLO-2019_273-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TOLO-2019-273">&#91;273&#93;</a></sup> which includes the state-owned <a href="/wiki/RTA_TV" class="mw-redirect" title="RTA TV">RTA TV</a> and various private channels such as <a href="/wiki/TOLO_(TV_channel)" title="TOLO (TV channel)">TOLO</a> and <a href="/wiki/Shamshad_TV" title="Shamshad TV">Shamshad TV</a>. The first Afghan newspaper was published in 1906,<sup id="cite_ref-Saikal2004_274-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Saikal2004-274">&#91;274&#93;</a></sup> and there are hundreds of print outlets today.<sup id="cite_ref-TOLO-2019_273-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TOLO-2019-273">&#91;273&#93;</a></sup> By the 1920s, <a href="/wiki/Radio_Kabul" title="Radio Kabul">Radio Kabul</a> was broadcasting local radio services.<sup id="cite_ref-Whitlock2003_275-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Whitlock2003-275">&#91;275&#93;</a></sup> Television programs began airing in the early 1970s. <a href="/wiki/Voice_of_America" title="Voice of America">Voice of America</a>, <a href="/wiki/BBC_World_Service" title="BBC World Service">BBC</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Radio_Free_Europe/Radio_Liberty" title="Radio Free Europe/Radio Liberty">Radio Free Europe/Radio Liberty</a> (RFE/RL) broadcast in both of Afghanistan's official languages.<sup id="cite_ref-276" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-276">&#91;276&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Since 2002, press restrictions have been gradually relaxed and private media diversified. <a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_expression" class="mw-redirect" title="Freedom of expression">Freedom of expression</a> and the press is promoted in the 2004 constitution, and censorship is banned, although <a href="/wiki/Defamation" title="Defamation">defaming</a> individuals or producing material contrary to the principles of Islam is prohibited.  In 2019, <a href="/wiki/Reporters_Without_Borders" title="Reporters Without Borders">Reporters Without Borders</a> listed the media environment of Afghanistan as 121st out of 179 on its <a href="/wiki/Press_Freedom_Index" title="Press Freedom Index">Press Freedom Index</a>, with 1st being most free.<sup id="cite_ref-277" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-277">&#91;277&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-278" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-278">&#91;278&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The city of Kabul has been home to many musicians who were masters of both traditional and modern <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Afghanistan" title="Music of Afghanistan">Afghan music</a>. Traditional music is especially popular during the <a href="/wiki/Nowruz" title="Nowruz">Nowruz</a> (New Year) and <a href="/wiki/Afghan_Independence_Day" title="Afghan Independence Day">National Independence Day</a> celebrations. <a href="/wiki/Ahmad_Zahir" title="Ahmad Zahir">Ahmad Zahir</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nashenas" title="Nashenas">Nashenas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mohammad_Hussain_Sarahang" title="Mohammad Hussain Sarahang">Ustad Sarahang</a>, <a href="/wiki/Abdul_Rahim_Sarban" title="Abdul Rahim Sarban">Sarban</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ubaidullah_Jan" title="Ubaidullah Jan">Ubaidullah Jan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Farhad_Darya" title="Farhad Darya">Farhad Darya</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Naghma" title="Naghma">Naghma</a> are some of the notable Afghan musicians, but there are many others.<sup id="cite_ref-279" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-279">&#91;279&#93;</a></sup> Afghans have long been accustomed to watching Indian <a href="/wiki/Bollywood" title="Bollywood">Bollywood</a> films and listening to its <a href="/wiki/Filmi" title="Filmi">filmi</a> songs. Many Bollywood film stars have roots in Afghanistan, including <a href="/wiki/Salman_Khan" title="Salman Khan">Salman Khan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saif_Ali_Khan" title="Saif Ali Khan">Saif Ali Khan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shah_Rukh_Khan" title="Shah Rukh Khan">Shah Rukh Khan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aamir_Khan" title="Aamir Khan">Aamir Khan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Feroz_Khan_(Indian_actor)" class="mw-redirect" title="Feroz Khan (Indian actor)">Feroz Khan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kader_Khan" title="Kader Khan">Kader Khan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Naseeruddin_Shah" title="Naseeruddin Shah">Naseeruddin Shah</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zarine_Khan" class="mw-redirect" title="Zarine Khan">Zarine Khan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Celina_Jaitly" title="Celina Jaitly">Celina Jaitly</a>, and a number of others. Several Bollywood films have been shot inside Afghanistan, including <i><a href="/wiki/Dharmatma" title="Dharmatma">Dharmatma</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Khuda_Gawah" title="Khuda Gawah">Khuda Gawah</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Escape_from_Taliban" title="Escape from Taliban">Escape from Taliban</a></i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/Kabul_Express" title="Kabul Express">Kabul Express</a></i>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Communication">Communication</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Communications_in_Afghanistan" title="Communications in Afghanistan">Communications in Afghanistan</a></div>
<p>Telecommunication services in Afghanistan are provided by <a href="/wiki/Afghan_Telecom" title="Afghan Telecom">Afghan Telecom</a>, <a href="/wiki/Afghan_Wireless" title="Afghan Wireless">Afghan Wireless</a>, <a href="/wiki/Etisalat" title="Etisalat">Etisalat</a>, <a href="/wiki/MTN_Group" title="MTN Group">MTN Group</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Roshan_(telco)" title="Roshan (telco)">Roshan</a>. The country uses its own space <a href="/wiki/Satellite" title="Satellite">satellite</a> called <a href="/wiki/Afghansat_1" title="Afghansat 1">Afghansat 1</a>, which provides services to millions of phone, internet, and television subscribers. By 2001 following years of civil war, telecommunications was virtually a non-existent sector, but by 2016 it had grown to a $2 billion industry, with 22 million mobile phone subscribers and 5 million internet users. The sector employs at least 120,000 people nationwide.<sup id="cite_ref-280" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-280">&#91;280&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Afghan_cuisine" title="Afghan cuisine">Afghan cuisine</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Afghan_cuisine.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Afghan_cuisine.jpg/250px-Afghan_cuisine.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="225" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Afghan_cuisine.jpg/375px-Afghan_cuisine.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Afghan_cuisine.jpg/500px-Afghan_cuisine.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="920" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Afghan_cuisine.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Some of the popular Afghan dishes</div></div></div>
<p>Afghan cuisine is largely based upon the nation's chief crops, such as <a href="/wiki/Wheat" title="Wheat">wheat</a>, <a href="/wiki/Maize" title="Maize">maize</a>, <a href="/wiki/Barley" title="Barley">barley</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rice" title="Rice">rice</a>. Accompanying these staples are native fruits and vegetables as well as dairy products such as <a href="/wiki/Milk" title="Milk">milk</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yogurt" title="Yogurt">yogurt</a> and <a href="/wiki/Whey" title="Whey">whey</a>. <a href="/wiki/Kabuli_palaw" title="Kabuli palaw">Kabuli palaw</a> is the <a href="/wiki/National_dish" title="National dish">national dish</a> of Afghanistan.<sup id="cite_ref-foodrepublic_281-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-foodrepublic-281">&#91;281&#93;</a></sup> The nation's culinary specialties reflect its ethnic and geographic diversity.<sup id="cite_ref-Brittin_282-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Brittin-282">&#91;282&#93;</a></sup> Afghanistan is known for its high quality <a href="/wiki/Pomegranate_production_in_Afghanistan" title="Pomegranate production in Afghanistan">pomegranates</a>, <a href="/wiki/Grape" title="Grape">grapes</a>, and sweet <a href="/wiki/Melon" title="Melon">melons</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-283" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-283">&#91;283&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Poetry">Poetry</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Poetry_of_Afghanistan" title="Poetry of Afghanistan">Poetry of Afghanistan</a></div>
<p>Classic <a href="/wiki/Persian_literature" title="Persian literature">Persian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pashto_literature_and_poetry" title="Pashto literature and poetry">Pashto poetry</a> are a cherished part of Afghan culture. Thursdays are traditionally "<a href="/wiki/Poetry" title="Poetry">poetry</a> night" in the city of <a href="/wiki/Herat" title="Herat">Herat</a> when men, women and children gather and recite both ancient and modern poems.<sup id="cite_ref-284" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-284">&#91;284&#93;</a></sup> Poetry has always been one of the major educational pillars in the region, to the level that it has integrated itself into culture. Some notable poets include <a href="/wiki/Rumi" title="Rumi">Rumi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rabi%27a_Balkhi" class="mw-redirect" title="Rabi&#39;a Balkhi">Rabi'a Balkhi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sanai" title="Sanai">Sanai</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jami" title="Jami">Jami</a>, <a href="/wiki/Khushal_Khan_Khattak" class="mw-redirect" title="Khushal Khan Khattak">Khushal Khan Khattak</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rahman_Baba" title="Rahman Baba">Rahman Baba</a>, <a href="/wiki/Khalilullah_Khalili" title="Khalilullah Khalili">Khalilullah Khalili</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Parween_Pazhwak" title="Parween Pazhwak">Parween Pazhwak</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-285" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-285">&#91;285&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sport_in_Afghanistan" title="Sport in Afghanistan">Sport in Afghanistan</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Zohib_Islam_Amiri_(in_red_uniform)_vs_Jeje_Lalpekhlua_(in_blue_uniform).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Zohib_Islam_Amiri_%28in_red_uniform%29_vs_Jeje_Lalpekhlua_%28in_blue_uniform%29.jpg/220px-Zohib_Islam_Amiri_%28in_red_uniform%29_vs_Jeje_Lalpekhlua_%28in_blue_uniform%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="166" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Zohib_Islam_Amiri_%28in_red_uniform%29_vs_Jeje_Lalpekhlua_%28in_blue_uniform%29.jpg/330px-Zohib_Islam_Amiri_%28in_red_uniform%29_vs_Jeje_Lalpekhlua_%28in_blue_uniform%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Zohib_Islam_Amiri_%28in_red_uniform%29_vs_Jeje_Lalpekhlua_%28in_blue_uniform%29.jpg/440px-Zohib_Islam_Amiri_%28in_red_uniform%29_vs_Jeje_Lalpekhlua_%28in_blue_uniform%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="610" data-file-height="459" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Zohib_Islam_Amiri_(in_red_uniform)_vs_Jeje_Lalpekhlua_(in_blue_uniform).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Afghanistan_national_football_team" title="Afghanistan national football team">Afghanistan national football team</a> (in red uniforms) before its first win over <a href="/wiki/India_national_football_team" title="India national football team">India</a> (in blue) during the <a href="/wiki/2011_SAFF_Championship" title="2011 SAFF Championship">2011 SAFF Championship</a>.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Nowruz_Buzkashi_Match_in_Mazar_(5778806122).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Nowruz_Buzkashi_Match_in_Mazar_%285778806122%29.jpg/200px-Nowruz_Buzkashi_Match_in_Mazar_%285778806122%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="149" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Nowruz_Buzkashi_Match_in_Mazar_%285778806122%29.jpg/300px-Nowruz_Buzkashi_Match_in_Mazar_%285778806122%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Nowruz_Buzkashi_Match_in_Mazar_%285778806122%29.jpg/400px-Nowruz_Buzkashi_Match_in_Mazar_%285778806122%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1874" data-file-height="1400" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Nowruz_Buzkashi_Match_in_Mazar_(5778806122).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The traditional national sport of Afghanistan, <a href="/wiki/Buzkashi" title="Buzkashi">Buzkashi</a></div></div></div>
<p>Sport in Afghanistan is managed by the <a href="/wiki/Afghan_Sports_Federation" title="Afghan Sports Federation">Afghan Sports Federation</a>. <a href="/wiki/Cricket" title="Cricket">Cricket</a> and <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">association football</a> are the two most popular sports in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-286" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-286">&#91;286&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-287" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-287">&#91;287&#93;</a></sup> The Afghan Sports Federation promotes cricket, association football, <a href="/wiki/Basketball" title="Basketball">basketball</a>, <a href="/wiki/Volleyball" title="Volleyball">volleyball</a>, <a href="/wiki/Golf" title="Golf">golf</a>, <a href="/wiki/Team_handball" class="mw-redirect" title="Team handball">handball</a>, <a href="/wiki/Boxing" title="Boxing">boxing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Taekwondo" title="Taekwondo">taekwondo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Olympic_weightlifting" title="Olympic weightlifting">weightlifting</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bodybuilding" title="Bodybuilding">bodybuilding</a>, <a href="/wiki/Track_and_field" title="Track and field">track and field</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ice_skating" title="Ice skating">skating</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bowling" title="Bowling">bowling</a>, <a href="/wiki/Snooker" title="Snooker">snooker</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chess" title="Chess">chess</a>, and other sports.
</p><p>Afghanistan's sports teams are increasingly celebrating titles at international events. Its <a href="/wiki/Afghanistan_national_basketball_team" title="Afghanistan national basketball team">basketball team</a> won the first team sports title at the <a href="/wiki/2010_South_Asian_Games" title="2010 South Asian Games">2010 South Asian Games</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-288" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-288">&#91;288&#93;</a></sup> Later that year, the country's <a href="/wiki/Afghanistan_national_cricket_team" title="Afghanistan national cricket team">cricket team</a> followed as it won the <a href="/wiki/2009%E2%80%9310_ICC_Intercontinental_Cup" title="2009–10 ICC Intercontinental Cup">2009–10 ICC Intercontinental Cup</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ICUP2009-10_289-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ICUP2009-10-289">&#91;289&#93;</a></sup> In 2012, the country's <a href="/wiki/Afghanistan_national_3x3_team" title="Afghanistan national 3x3 team">3x3 basketball team</a> won the gold medal at the <a href="/wiki/3-on-3_basketball_at_the_2012_Asian_Beach_Games" class="mw-redirect" title="3-on-3 basketball at the 2012 Asian Beach Games">2012 Asian Beach Games</a>. In 2013, Afghanistan's <a href="/wiki/Afghanistan_national_football_team" title="Afghanistan national football team">football team</a> followed as it won the <a href="/wiki/SAFF_Championship" title="SAFF Championship">SAFF Championship</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-SAFF2013_290-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SAFF2013-290">&#91;290&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Afghanistan_national_cricket_team" title="Afghanistan national cricket team">Afghan national cricket team</a>, which was formed in 2001, participated in the <a href="/wiki/2009_ICC_World_Cup_Qualifier" class="mw-redirect" title="2009 ICC World Cup Qualifier">2009 ICC World Cup Qualifier</a>, <a href="/wiki/2010_ICC_World_Cricket_League_Division_One" title="2010 ICC World Cricket League Division One">2010 ICC World Cricket League Division One</a> and the <a href="/wiki/2010_ICC_World_Twenty20" title="2010 ICC World Twenty20">2010 ICC World Twenty20</a>. It won the <a href="/wiki/ACC_Twenty20_Cup" title="ACC Twenty20 Cup">ACC Twenty20 Cup</a> in 2007, 2009, 2011 and 2013. The team eventually made it and played in the <a href="/wiki/2015_Cricket_World_Cup" title="2015 Cricket World Cup">2015 Cricket World Cup</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-291" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-291">&#91;291&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Afghanistan_Cricket_Board" title="Afghanistan Cricket Board">Afghanistan Cricket Board</a> (ACB) is the official governing body of the sport and is headquartered in Kabul. The <a href="/wiki/Alokozay_Kabul_International_Cricket_Ground" title="Alokozay Kabul International Cricket Ground">Alokozay Kabul International Cricket Ground</a> serves as the nation's main cricket stadium. There are several other stadiums throughout the country, including the <a href="/wiki/Ghazi_Amanullah_Khan_International_Cricket_Stadium" class="mw-redirect" title="Ghazi Amanullah Khan International Cricket Stadium">Ghazi Amanullah Khan International Cricket Stadium</a> near <a href="/wiki/Jalalabad" title="Jalalabad">Jalalabad</a>. Domestically, cricket is played between teams from different provinces.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Afghanistan_national_football_team" title="Afghanistan national football team">Afghanistan national football team</a> has been competing in international <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">football</a> since 1941.<sup id="cite_ref-292" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-292">&#91;292&#93;</a></sup> The national team plays its home games at the <a href="/wiki/Ghazi_Stadium" title="Ghazi Stadium">Ghazi Stadium</a> in Kabul, while <a href="/wiki/Football_in_Afghanistan" title="Football in Afghanistan">football in Afghanistan</a> is governed by the <a href="/wiki/Afghanistan_Football_Federation" title="Afghanistan Football Federation">Afghanistan Football Federation</a>. The national team has never competed or qualified for the <a href="/wiki/FIFA_World_Cup" title="FIFA World Cup">FIFA World Cup</a> but has recently won an international football trophy in 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-SAFF2013_290-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SAFF2013-290">&#91;290&#93;</a></sup> The country also has a national team in the sport of futsal, a 5-a-side variation of football.
</p><p>The traditional and the national sport of Afghanistan is <a href="/wiki/Buzkashi" title="Buzkashi">buzkashi</a>, mainly popular among the northern Afghans. It is similar to <a href="/wiki/Polo" title="Polo">polo</a>, played by horsemen in two teams, each trying to grab and hold a goat carcass.<sup id="cite_ref-twsj_293-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-twsj-293">&#91;293&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Afghan_Hound" title="Afghan Hound">Afghan Hound</a> (a type of running dog) originated in Afghanistan and was formerly used in <a href="/wiki/Wolf_hunting_with_dogs" title="Wolf hunting with dogs">wolf hunting</a>.  In 2002, traveler <a href="/wiki/Rory_Stewart" title="Rory Stewart">Rory Stewart</a> reported that dogs were still used for wolf hunting in remote areas.<sup id="cite_ref-294" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-294">&#91;294&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<li id="cite_note-10"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-10">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The phoneme <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/f/</span> <span style="font-size:140%;">ف</span> occurs only in loanwords in Pashto, it tends to be replaced with <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/p/</span> <span style="font-size:140%;">پ</span>. <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[b]</span> is also an allophone of <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/p/</span> before voiced consonants; <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">[v]</span> is an allophone of <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/f/</span> before voiced consonants in loanwords.</span>
