<li id="cite_note-Hyman2016-68"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Hyman2016_68-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation book">Anthony Hyman (27 July 2016). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/?id=nvO-DAAAQBAJ&amp;pg=PA46&amp;lpg=PA46&amp;dq=afghanistan+japan+germany+partition#v=onepage&amp;q=afghanistan%20japan%20germany%20partition&amp;f=false"><i>Afghanistan under Soviet Domination, 1964–91</i></a>. <li id="cite_note-Bowersox-69"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Bowersox_69-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation book">Bowersox, Gary W. (2004). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=WVAN9pjnRzMC&amp;pg=PA100"><i>The Gem Hunter: The Adventures of an American in Afghanistan</i></a>. United States: GeoVision, Inc. p.&#160;100. <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-0-9747323-1-2" title="Special:BookSources/978-0-9747323-1-2"><bdi>978-0-9747323-1-2</bdi></a>. <q>To launch this plan, Bhutto recruited and trained a group of Afghans in the <a href="/wiki/Bala_Hissar,_Peshawar" title="Bala Hissar, Peshawar">Bala-Hesar</a> of <a href="/wiki/Peshawar" title="Peshawar">Peshawar</a>, in Pakistan's <a href="/wiki/Khyber_Pakhtunkhwa" title="Khyber Pakhtunkhwa">North-west Frontier Province</a>. Among these young men were <a href="/wiki/Ahmad_Shah_Massoud" title="Ahmad Shah Massoud">Massoud</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gulbuddin_Hekmatyar" title="Gulbuddin Hekmatyar">Gulbuddin Hekmatyar</a>, and other members of Jawanan-e Musulman. Massoud's mission to Bhutto was to create unrest in northern Afghanistan. It served Massoud's interests, which were opposition to the Soviets and independence for Afghanistan. Later, after Massoud and Hekmatyar had a terrible falling-out over Massoud's opposition to terrorist tactics and methods, Massoud overthrew from Jawanan-e Musulman. He joined <a href="/wiki/Burhanuddin_Rabbani" title="Burhanuddin Rabbani">Rabani</a>'s newly created Afghan political party, <a href="/wiki/Jamiat-e_Islami" title="Jamiat-e Islami">Jamiat-i-Islami</a>, in exile in <a href="/wiki/Pakistan" title="Pakistan">Pakistan</a>.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=The+Gem+Hunter%3A+The+Adventures+of+an+American+in+Afghanistan&amp;rft.place=United+States&amp;rft.pages=100&amp;rft.pub=GeoVision%2C+Inc.&amp;rft.date=2004&amp;rft.isbn=978-0-9747323-1-2&amp;rft.aulast=Bowersox&amp;rft.aufirst=Gary+W.&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3DWVAN9pjnRzMC%26pg%3DPA100&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AAfghanistan" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886058088"/></span>

<li id="cite_note-Kakar-80"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Kakar_80-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation book">Kakar, Mohammed (3 March 1997). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://publishing.cdlib.org/ucpressebooks/view?docId=ft7b69p12h;brand=ucpress"><i>The Soviet Invasion and the Afghan Response, 1979–1982</i></a>. University of California Press. <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9780520208933" title="Special:BookSources/9780520208933"><bdi>9780520208933</bdi></a>. <q>The Afghans are among the latest victims of genocide by a superpower. Large numbers of Afghans were killed to suppress resistance to the army of the Soviet Union, which wished to vindicate its client regime and realize its goal in Afghanistan.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=The+Soviet+Invasion+and+the+Afghan+Response%2C+1979%E2%80%931982&amp;rft.pub=University+of+California+Press&amp;rft.date=1997-03-03&amp;rft.isbn=9780520208933&amp;rft.aulast=Kakar&amp;rft.aufirst=Mohammed&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fpublishing.cdlib.org%2Fucpressebooks%2Fview%3FdocId%3Dft7b69p12h%3Bbrand%3Ducpress&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AAfghanistan" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886058088"/></span>

<li id="cite_note-81"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-81">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation book">Klass, Rosanne (1994). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=I2chrSJCW54C&amp;pg=PA129"><i>The Widening Circle of Genocide</i></a>. Transaction Publishers. p.&#160;129. <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-1-4128-3965-5" title="Special:BookSources/978-1-4128-3965-5"><bdi>978-1-4128-3965-5</bdi></a>. <q>During the intervening fourteen years of Communist rule, an estimated 1.5 to 2 million Afghan civilians were killed by Soviet forces and their proxies- the four Communist regimes in Kabul, and the East Germans, Bulgarians, Czechs, Cubans, Palestinians, Indians and others who assisted them. These were not battle casualties or the unavoidable civilian victims of warfare. Soviet and local Communist forces seldom attacked the scattered guerilla bands of the Afghan Resistance except, in a few strategic locales like the Panjsher valley. Instead they deliberately targeted the civilian population, primarily in the rural areas.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=The+Widening+Circle+of+Genocide&amp;rft.pages=129&amp;rft.pub=Transaction+Publishers&amp;rft.date=1994&amp;rft.isbn=978-1-4128-3965-5&amp;rft.aulast=Klass&amp;rft.aufirst=Rosanne&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3DI2chrSJCW54C%26pg%3DPA129&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AAfghanistan" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886058088"/></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-Reisman-82"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Reisman_82-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web">Reisman, W. Michael; Norchi, Charles H. <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.paulbogdanor.com/left/afghan/genocide.pdf">"Genocide and the Soviet Occupation of Afghanistan"</a> <span class="cs1-format">(PDF)</span><span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">7 January</span> 2017</span>. <q>According to widely reported accounts, substantial programmes of depopulation have been conducted in these Afghan provinces: Ghazni, Nagarhar, Lagham, Qandahar, Zabul, Badakhshan, Lowgar, Paktia, Paktika and Kunar...There is considerable evidence that genocide has been committed against the Afghan people by the combined forces of the Democratic Republic of Afghanistan and the Soviet Union.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.btitle=Genocide+and+the+Soviet+Occupation+of+Afghanistan&amp;rft.aulast=Reisman&amp;rft.aufirst=W.+Michael&amp;rft.au=Norchi%2C+Charles+H.&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.paulbogdanor.com%2Fleft%2Fafghan%2Fgenocide.pdf&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AAfghanistan" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886058088"/></span>
</li>

<li id="cite_note-Public_Opinion-122"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Public_Opinion_122-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://acsor-surveys.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/01/Afghan-Futures-Wave-6-Analysis_FINAL-v2.pdf">"Afghan Futures: A National Public Opinion Survey"</a> <span class="cs1-format">(PDF)</span>. 29 January 2015. p.&#160;4<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">2 January</span> 2017</span>. <q>Seventy-seven percent support the presence of U.S. forces; 67 percent say the same of NATO/ISAF forces more generally. Despite the country’s travails, eight in 10 say it was a good thing for the United States to oust the Taliban in 2001. And much more blame either the Taliban or al Qaeda for the country’s violence, 53 percent, than blame the United States, 12 percent. The latter is about half what it was in 2012, coinciding with a sharp reduction in the U.S. deployment.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.btitle=Afghan+Futures%3A+A+National+Public+Opinion+Survey&amp;rft.pages=4&amp;rft.date=2015-01-29&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Facsor-surveys.com%2Fwp-content%2Fuploads%2F2015%2F01%2FAfghan-Futures-Wave-6-Analysis_FINAL-v2.pdf&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AAfghanistan" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886058088"/></span>
